# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Produce answer.json** — Write ALL output to `/workspace/answer.json` with this structure:
   ```json
   {
     "analysis": {
       "summary": "Brief description of your approach",
       "files_examined": [{"path": "file.ext", "description": "..."}],
       "reasoning": "Detailed explanation or analysis"
     },
     "changes": [
       {"file": "path.ext", "description": "...", "diff": "unified diff"}
     ]
   }
   ```
   Omit `changes` if the task is analysis-only. Do NOT edit source files directly — produce diffs in `changes[]` instead.

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

# Django ORM Raw SQL Injection Prevention

## Your Task

Find all Python source files in django/django that handle raw SQL queries and prevent SQL injection: the RawSQL expression sanitization, the raw() queryset method parameter binding, and the cursor.execute() parameterization enforcement.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/django--674eda1c.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/django--674eda1c` (django/django)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

74-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of Django's SQL injection prevention mechanisms for raw SQL queries. The answer has been written to `/workspace/answer.json` with:

## Summary of Findings

**6 Key Files** implementing SQL injection prevention:
1. `django/db/models/expressions.py` - RawSQL class
2. `django/db/models/query.py` - raw() and extra() methods, RawQuerySet class
3. `django/db/models/sql/query.py` - RawQuery class with execution logic
4. `django/db/models/sql/where.py` - ExtraWhere parameter binding
5. `django/db/backends/utils.py` - CursorWrapper parameterization enforcement
6. `django/db/backends/base/operations.py` - Parameter type adaptation

**12 Key Symbols** that prevent SQL injection:
- `RawSQL` expression class for sanitized raw SQL
- `QuerySet.raw()` and `QuerySet.extra()` methods
- `RawQuerySet` and `RawQuery` classes
- `RawQuery._execute_query()` - the critical execution point
- `Query.check_alias()` and `Query.add_extra()` for validation
- `CursorWrapper.execute()` - parameterization enforcement
- `ExtraWhere` class for parameter binding

**Execution Chain**: QuerySet.raw() → RawQuerySet → RawQuery._execute_query() → CursorWrapper.execute()

**Three Key Defense Mechanisms**:
1. **Parameter Separation** - SQL and parameters kept separate throughout the chain
2. **Database Driver Parameterization** - Parameters passed as separate arguments to cursor.execute()
3. **Alias Validation** - Column aliases validated against FORBIDDEN_ALIAS_PATTERN to block injection attempts

Because HTTPS\\n85: provides additional security, it is imperative to ensure connections use HTTPS\\n86: where it is available by forwarding insecure connection requests and using\\n87: HSTS for supported browsers.\\n88: \\n89: Be very careful with marking views with the ``csrf_exempt`` decorator unless\\n90: it is absolutely necessary.\\n91: \\n92: .. _sql-injection-protection:\\n93: \\n94: SQL injection protection\\n95: ========================\\n96: \\n97: SQL injection is a type of attack where a malicious user is able to execute\\n98: arbitrary SQL code on a database. This can result in records\\n99: being deleted or data leakage.\\n100: \\n101: Django's querysets are protected from SQL injection since their queries are\\n102: constructed using query parameterization. A query's SQL code is defined\\n103: separately from the query's parameters. Since parameters may be user-provided\\n104: and therefore unsafe, they are escaped by the underlying database driver.\\n105: \\n106: Django also gives developers power to write :ref:`raw queries\\n107: <executing-raw-queries>` or execute :ref:`custom sql <executing-custom-sql>`.\\n108: These capabilities should be used sparingly and you should always be careful to\\n109: properly escape any parameters that the user can control. Its __init__ takes both sql and params arguments, and the as_sql() method returns the SQL string with params as a separate tuple, enabling proper parameterization at the database driver level.\n\n## raw() QuerySet Method (django/db/models/query.py:1461-1473)\nThe raw() method accepts raw_query and params arguments, creating a RawQuerySet instance.
